<Date>1547618731636<//Date><response>None<//response><Review>Terra Sushi is a great option for lunch or dinner sushi if the food quality is your primary concern. If possible I would rate 4.5 stars only deducting for the size of the in-restaurant dining compared to other sushi options in the area.

This next statement is entirely debatable and my own personal opinion. I put it here only to ensure that this review is only valued if read in a TIMELY manner. I am of the personal opinion that sushi places have the best quality fish at the beginning of their existence and tend to degrade over time as they make the trade off between cost and reputation. I will do my best to update this review if I notice a change in Terra's food or service as clearly from my rating I intend to be a repeat customer.

Because there are so many different preferences in "sushi" I think it is important to quickly describe my personal preferences. I am unquestionably "American" in my preferences in that I prefer "sushi" to have multiple layers of flavor, and evaluate it based on the quality of each ingredient included in the roll I ordered. While I can enjoy sashimi (although my preferred style is nigiri), if I order a roll with multiple ingredients I expect EVERY ingredient to be of similar quality. Many sushi places pay a lot of attention to one ingredient but seem to devalue others. Terra pretty clearly completely understands the construction of sushi "soup to nuts". I could very happily order a bowl of sushi (meaning only the vinegrated rice) take it home and construct my own rolls and be happy with the value.

They have a good offering of the carnival style rolls many Americans have come to expect, and everything else I would expect from another similar sushi joint with the exception of steak options. I don't mind this (and in fact respect the limited options similar to In-N-Out) as they seem to be just trying to stay in their lane. Teriyaki Chicken however was refreshing in that is was a little watery and soy-based rather than some of the sugary styles out there. As far as service, I have not actually dined IN the restaurant. If the wife and I actually get a night out without kids, I am looking for a little more ambiance and would likely be willing to gamble a bit on quality to get a more robust "dine in" experience. While picking up my orders however, this has struck me as a great place for an efficient dining experience when running behind for a movie rather than a place I could happily spend 1.5 hours.

Between Einstein's Bagels next door (for light breakfast), Baja Fish Tacos for lunch, and this....I could happily eat three meals in one day in this center.< /Review><UserId.>108731747713367167122< /UserId.>< user_name>

< Text>
I've been to Trout Creek Rec Center many times while renting summer houses in Tahoe Donner. It's a giant disappointment & really misses the potential it could have to be the only resort / rec center in the North Tahoe area. Here are the reasons why: the price is astronomical & sets the guest up to expect great things when paying the (reduced) rate of $15 per person (kids over age 6 have to pay the adult rate). Then, Trout Creek fails to meet even modest expectations. 1) staff ranges from unhelpful to rude. Need a towel? They're part of the price of admission, but they won't tell you that. They are kept behind the counter at the front desk. 2) As of 2019, the place is under massive construction & half of it is closed. They do not tell you this when taking your payment. What's worse? The construction is happening while the place is open. Buzz saws, hard hat areas, and literally a guy painting the ceiling as we walked under it! 3) The new sauna room smells like MRSA lying in wait 4) The pool itself is "kind of" clean in certain areas. In one large corner, pollen and dead bugs gather and it has always been this way. 5) Exercise classes are subpar; don't waste your money. I saw an instructor  doing leg lifts on all fours with a sway back. 6) The pool is cold all summer long.  One good thing about the facility is when Marco Polo Grill is open -- they offer poolside food service. It's fun and pretty tasty. However, they keep limited hours and don't open until late June.</Text>

I rated 4/5 and had a very good visit.

Pros - Nice environment with with a friendly staff. The office has a corky theme that dosent take itself too seriously. The staff and office were nice and very good with the kids. I never felt rushed, pressured or like "Just another patient".

Cons - The proccess was abit slow and some of the questions were abit personal. I felt like the staff was abit relaxed and the process was different than usual. I wasnt quite aware of some of the add-ons unitl I asked (Lenses) and my daughter loved kid frames but the size was wrong.

Summary - 5 stars would be VERY hard for me to give anyone. This place faced some obstacles with my visit but adapted at every turn. Even when my daughters frames didnt fit they dug into a shipment they just recieved. The lens person was very knowledgeable about any questions asked and even demonstrated differences. The eye doctor was equally knowledgeable and made the visit feel personally taylored to me. Thank you guys for finding a way to make my flex delay work and the outstanding visit.

Edit*
We were contacted Thursday or so. After paying a little over 1200.00 on monday I thought my glasses were in. I called nack Saturday only to be told that due to a misunderstanding my glasses were just being proccessed on Saturday. So even though the office got their money and messed up my 10 day wait started 6 days later.

No mention of anything to compensate or make things right. Appreantly once they have your money any burdens thereafter are all yours.

<review>To preface, great place for really good sandwiches. Order the Dutch Crunch bread, it's baked by Ike's with their specialty "dirty sauce" baked in.

I dont know why "College Students" is a Yelp 'Highlight' for this place, or at all. Why is "College Students" a highlight- no, what is that even supposed to mean? Whatever..
You want sandwiches? They got sandwiches! You need an ol' fashioned soda? bAm, they got your sodas right here. This place is expensive, yes. It's also expensive in Danville, Concord, Walnut Creek and SFSU; it's because it's worth it if you truly value your sammy! The tastiest of samwiches sold here!</review>< pictures>

<GmapID>0x808f77cafd393e41:0xccecea040133750e<//GmapID><time>1549968577193< /time>< Text>
Conveniently located not too far coming off the highway on Rollins. I came here for a party and everyone had a blast. All of us never played baseball and the staff was pretty good about teaching us the basics and up to speed quickly.

The staff is also very nice, patient, and attentive... taking care of our party. You can choose to hit baseballs or softballs and choose the speed. Interestingly enough, the speeds are actually higher than stated because how close the ball-shooter is to you, so think about that when choosing your speed!

Would recommend and be back!<//Text>

<review>Good bang for your buck.  This is just based on pricing for the BP cages.  You can get 20 rounds of 20 balls for $60.  These are dimpled balls so bring an aluminum bat, they have some there you can borrow.  Can't use wood bats and I've heard composites can get damaged with dimpled balls (if you want to practice with hard balls there are other more expensive places).  BIG BONUS - They have a simulated pitcher image with full motion to help kids timing, this is very rare in other places where you just get the std pitching machine.

From an instructional standpoint, you can't beat Terry for hitting.  Obviously the only MLB player on the Peninsula that has his own cage, so his instruction is going to be a bit more expensive than other places.  Well worth it for kids that are already physically coordinated.</review>< userid>
